O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and the fullness of the medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications. And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of surgery, that is to say "surgery."
And because the practice of surgery is forbidden in our region and is completely banned everywhere, the science has perished and disappeared, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors that have been handled by hands (i.e. copied). And because of this, errors and false beliefs have arisen, and understanding has been closed off and the knowledge has been distanced.
It seems to me that I wish to gather together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will gather together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the explanation and preparation of them, as is necessary.
And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is diminished. And it is necessary for one who practices (medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they know precisely the members (of the body), and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of orifices, and the operation and moving and resting veins, and where they originate.
And so Hippocrates said that a name without (corresponding) work is much, and in the art of surgery it is little.[ note: this quote means that having knowledge without putting it into practice is not enough, especially in the medical field. ]
We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things should be careful not to fall into error and not to kill people; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science without knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula in a woman's neck and cut the arteries of her neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman died in his hands.
And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took away a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died three days later.
And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it out, he would die.
And see one other doctor who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break also had a wound; and the ignorant doctor tightly binds the break over the wound with bandages, and left no cloth on the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg was completely swollen and the foot became lost.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind his leg; and when I had undone it, he was calm and felt no pain.
But in any case, the corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the entire limb was lost.
And I saw another doctor who lanced a boil that had become hardened and then inflamed it due to his lack of skill.
Because gangrene, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not at all be touched with iron if the entire corrupt part cannot be completely removed from such a place.
And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work in which there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
So take up your weapons in cotton and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best approach so that through the grace of God you may come to safety and be praised; and leave behind dreadful diseases with serious consequences; and put aside your weapons from what causes doubt in you, and have faith in yourself so that you can journey from this world to the other world of glory.
Galen says in one of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a serious illness, for you will be called a foolish fool."[In other words, it is unwise to attempt to treat a severe or hopeless disease without the proper knowledge and skills, as doing so may result in failure and ridicule.]
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medical caustics, and this chapter is organized from head to toe; it includes the forms of instruments, iron tools for cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter includes the forms of instruments
The third chapter is about reducing dislocations and sprains, and similar things; it is organized from head to toe and includes the forms of instruments.[3](https://hyp.is/Qr6E0-pWEeyv8k1sXgx4Pw/www.oldfrench-medieval.com/medicine/treatise/traite_de_cirurgie_medievale_extraits.html)
In order to remind ourselves of the work, it is necessary for me to describe the qualities of the help and harm of each complexion.
I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest to speak of, and a subtle science and hidden knowledge; and of this, many sages have spoken and agreed upon; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I dread the lengthiness.
I say that cautery helps universally in all constitutions where there is matter, except for two constitutions: namely, the hot constitution without matter, and the dry constitution without matter.
In the hot and dry constitution together with matter, some have divided and said that cautery is of great help there; and others have said the contrary: that cautery is of no value for disease that comes from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot and it should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat, nor by dryness; and he who says the contrary says that cautery provides great help for hot and dry disease in the human body.[8] For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true through experience.
And yet, only those who have experienced it and understand through long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of human complexions, as well as the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and seasonal variations should involve themselves with it; we are not afraid of other complexions, even cold and moist ones. And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
And know, son, that fire cautery is among the useful treatments for wounds, and of greater goodness than blistering with hot medicine.
For fire is simple and only affects the member that is burned, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to do so.
Hot medicines spread from member to another and can bring illness with difficult healing, and perhaps even kill the patient.
Fire, because of its greatness and the goodness of its substance, does not cause this harm unless there is excess.
And this I have found through experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret which is hidden in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it undoes the sicknesses of bodies, as the philosophers say in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauteries should be performed and chose priests.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm that may occur is prevented by the aid of the cautery; and even if the cautery is necessary to alleviate urgent and severe pain that cannot wait for the time when greater harm does not come to the limb.
And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; for there is no return of the disease that is healed by cautery; and they say this; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not only a medicine that changes the complexion, but also dries out the humors that are the cause of pain, and is worth more than other medicines due to its quickness and effectiveness.
And it is possible that the illness comes to the patient according to their constitution and the location of the disease and its strength; and harmful excesses are gathered in them through the acquisition of foods and similar things, if cauteries are not administered in places where there are little excess and moisture, such as cauteries of dens for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the "last resort" of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cauteries are effective after medical treatments, but their belief is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures in any disease and they are not effective, then we administer cautery, and it is effective. Then it becomes clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the belief of foolish physicians.
The ancients said that cauteries with instruments of gold are more effective than those of iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. And they said that the location of the cautery does not cause gangrene, but this is not true as I have experienced and found it to be true in some men; and cauteries of gold are more effective than those of iron, just as they claimed.
And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it has soon cooled down; and if one heats it too much, they burn it in the fire; and thus there are enough hindrances.
And for this reason we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to foot, so that the vein may be easier to find.[IS
The olive cautery
This cautery is effective for moisture and coldness on the skull, and there are two types that are done for a disease called "soda," and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coldness, such as paralysis and stiffness and apoplexy and similar diseases.
The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine that clears the head, three or four times, according to what the patient's strength, water content, and habit can tolerate; and then heat up the patient's head.
And then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands and place their hands on something heavy; after that, put the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and where your middle fingers meet, bleed by making an incision, then heat up the "olivare" cautery, which looks like this:
And place the cautery on the mark made with ink, and move your hand downward and outward in small circular motions; then quickly remove your hand, and check to see if you can see a small white spot of bone; and if not, continue applying the cautery until you do see the bone as I have instructed; after that, take a little bit of salt and place it in warm water with soft cotton, and put it on the mark, and leave it there for three days; after that, put wet cotton soaked in butter on top, and leave it on until the heat is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it heals.
And so said the ancients, that the longer a wound stays open, the more it purges; and therefore, it heals better.
And some said that one should let the cautery burn long enough that a part of the bone is burnt, then remove what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.
And others said that one should leave the cautery on for so long and press down so hard that it creates a hole as wide as a finger ring, like the ones women wear in their ears to let out humors; and then one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, it should be cured and bound up.
And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except for certain people who are in danger; and it seems to me that I should choose the second method; for the wound becomes weakened by continuous discharges due to natural processes, as we have observed in other limbs; and even when the patient's wound is naturally weak, the first cautery seems safer and more effective to me; and with this one, I perform my treatment for a speedy recovery.
of ancient head pain.
When chronic pain comes all over the head and lasts long, the patient should use ear drops and pills called "cochie," and purges of the head and eyes and poultices; and if they perform the cautery as we have previously said, and it is ineffective.
Take care if the patient's headache is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly under the cautery that we have mentioned earlier.
After this, perform cautery on each temple of the head down to the bone, as we have previously said, and make a cautery at the spot called "vasselz"; it is a place where cups are put; and be gentle with your hand so that you do not go all the way down to the bone: the patient will feel much more pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of that later; and the cauteries at the temples should be finer than those used for the center of the head, and here is the method:
of the head cautery When in a part of the head sudden pain comes, and the sickness extends to the eye, and the temple is purged with cleansing medicines, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help at all: then cauterization is done in two ways, namely with agury medicine and fire.
The cautery of agury medicine is: take a piece of aloe wood, remove the bark and soak it in a little bit of water for two temples, then make an incision in the temple where the pain resides, in such a way that you can place the piece of aloe wood beneath the skin; and when it is placed, bind and hold it tight and leave it like that for twelve hours; then loosen and remove the piece of aloe wood, and let the wound remain like that for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
After the treatment with ointment until it heals; and if you wish, then use some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatment of burning medicines.
The fire cautery is done in this manner: heat the cautery, which has this shape: (image)
And it is called "clos" because the head has the shape of a bell with one curved part, and in the middle there is a small protrusion; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn it slightly, lightly, until half of the thickness of the flesh is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and let there be an abundant flow of blood.
Afterward, place cotton soaked in oil on it, and leave it on for three days; then apply moistened cotton with butter, and then cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this headache with the "cultellare" cautery, at its entire tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
The word "emigraine" in the medieval medical text refers to a type of headache or migraine. It is an archaic term that is no longer used in modern medicine.
When you treat migraines as we have said in the previous division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the previous cautery medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the "cultellare" cautery until it is white; and then gently pass it over the painful area a line half a finger-width long, and remove your hand once, and be careful not to cover the artery and not to reach the bone; and watch out for the jaw which moves when eating, and make sure that the nerve does not move and that spasms do not come to the patient, and watch out for bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear even for those who are unaware and untrained; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it belongs.
And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is bearable, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautioner that we have mentioned in the chapter on arrow extraction, with the cautioner that has two blades; and this cautioner is better than the other and more helpful.
of ear pain due to cold dampness
When there is ear pain due to cold and you have worked on it with solvents and other cures as we have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "pounce" which looks like this:
After that, puncture all around the affected ear, or both if the pain is in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after marking the incision site; and have ten punctures around each ear; then cure the area until it is healed.
of the torture of the mouth
A torture that should be cured by cautery is only one that moves fluids, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
When you cure this type of torture that moves fluid from sweating and cleanings of the head and gargling, and if it is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third on the jawline between the two lips; and place the cautery on the visible healthy part, and cauterize near the head of the ear a little above and below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a small piece; and leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burned; and this is the method of cauterization:
And this is the type of cutting that we have mentioned before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be slightly larger; after curing the wound as I have said before until it heals.[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89tymologie_de_l'expression_%22au_bout_du_tunnel%22)
When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient does not have a fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery at the back of the mouth of the stomach; and cure it as we have said before.
of diarrhea
For this illness, give the patient large and pure pills to cleanse the brain; then shave the patient's head and apply the plaster of sinapi, which is written in the treatise on plasters, to the back of their head; and this is the method of cautery: do as I have said.
If the patient is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, perform three cauteries along the scalp, descending to the neck, with two finger-widths of space between each cautery; treat it as you would other injuries, and if you see fit, add one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns (temples), and continue treatment until they are healed; and use the cautery called "olivare," as I have previously mentioned.
of the coldness (or numbness) of the head. It is necessary that the head be cleaned of humors and things previously mentioned; after heating the patient's head, then perform cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, one at the back and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient tolerant, and the illness is severe, perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be for as long as the deepest flesh is burnt, then remove your hand; after that, heal until it is healed, and use the cure called "olivare" that we mentioned before.
About epilepsy.
Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain of humors and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and tolerant of taking medicine.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, perform gargling and chewing to cleanse the brain frequently with good meats; after heating the head in the middle, then perform one cautery according to what we have said before, and one on the fontanel, and on each temple; and if the patient is severe and tolerant, perform cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and weakness of body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have mentioned.
If the patient is young, perform one subtle cautery in the following manner:
When, due to melancholy, there are corrupt superfluities or thick phlegm, then apply several cauteries as we have said to the one who has paralysis.
And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities are inclined towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them to drink something that will purify the brain, according to what has been previously divided (explained) in the text.[1](footnote-1)
After that, anoint the patient's head; then make a well-made linen roll in the shape of a circle and place it on their head, with the patient lying crosswise and held securely from all sides. Then present the liniment and warm it with moderately hot butter from old herbs; then heat the cloth so that the skin can tolerate it. Afterward, remove the circle from inside the head and let it cool down, and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatments until they are healed.
Or, if you wish to cauterize by making several holes with the entire cautery, this method of cauterization moistens the brain greatly. Then place a cotton swab soaked in butter and goose fat on top.[1](footnote-1)
of the evacuation of the eyes When evacuation first occurs in the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something that purifies the head and guards against all moisture, and make them sweat or take several baths while fasting.
Afterwards, have them tilt their head back, and apply a cautery to the head, and make two cauterizations on the temples if the descent of the evacuation is in both eyes together or in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are underneath the skull, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for blood loss, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can.
And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incisions, how to stretch them with caution; and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is applied underneath the two bones at the back.
of the body of tears
When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids, phlegmatic; then do the cautery that I have said in the beginning descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the eye socket below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
of the body of tears inside the eyes
When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three mouthfuls of cooked wine; then raise the head, and do cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and do two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery. And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery called "olivary," which has the following form:
And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two pimples as long as they are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the paper is burnt, in the manner that I have said.
the hair that pricks the eye Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are performed in two ways: that is, with fire or with a burning medicine.[I have translated "cauteres" as "cauteries" because the word refers to the medical procedure of cauterization.]
For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the eyelashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
When they (the hairs) grow and are even, then place the patient in a upright position; afterward, on a piece of paper place a mark that is similar to the shape of a fern leaf, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered perilla leaves on the eye, then heat up the cautery with the following shape:
After cauterizing in the marked shape many times, so that the skin is burned, a sign of the success of the procedure is if you see the paper retracted and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eyelid; then lift your hand and leave it like this for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if after this the hairs return and the paper has softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot as before; and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the paper returns to its natural position and is even, without any hair touching the eye.
The fire cautery of medicine is when you instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then take a piece of parchment and shape it like a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and do this quickly so that it does not cool; then spread it on the shaped form as you have made it, like the fern leaf, and place it over the paper of the eyes; if the illness is only in one eye, then work on one side, and if in both, then also; and put cotton soaked in egg white underneath the eye; and the patient's head should be upright and your hand should be pressing on the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, for they will feel a burning sensation as if from fire. When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from its place. And when the biting (of the cautery) has passed, lift the lifting stick and look to see if you see the skin lifted as if it had been lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then place a moistened cotton compress on the burnt area until the burn has cooled. Afterwards, cure the site of the ointment (the burn) called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
And if it is necessary for you to be vigilant in your work and take great care that no medicine gets into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft (or "mole" in Old French) afterwards, and hairs prick in the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area where the skin has softened properly, just as you did before; after that, cure it until it is healed. This is the form of the leaf of the remedy.[ OPEN AI PROMPT COMPLETIONS MAY BE INACCURATE AND SHOULD ONLY BE USED AS A GUIDE TO WRITING THE FINAL TRANSLATION. ]
And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and accordingly you should adjust your constraints (or "constraignemens" in Old French); and do not apply the same strict rules to those who study this art as others.
of the treatment of fistula by cautery
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on it in this manner.
Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have a minister hold their head between your hands so that it does not move or leave its position. Afterwards, apply a cotton swab dipped in egg white or parsley juice on the eye. Then heat up the cautery tool which is shaped like a rooster's spur, bring it to the patient's head with the tip of the spur facing forward, and make sure that the cauter is sharpened from one end to the other. Alternatively, you can shape it like a tent, but in any case, ensure that it is sharp enough for your task.
Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove any pus or dry matter from it. If it is closed, then open it up and remove the blockage. Then place hot bran on top of the cautery tool, and hold your hand with the cautery to the white part near the eye, but be careful not to move your hand excessively. Next, apply the cautery tool to the fatty tissue around the eye and allow it to corrupt (i.e. burn).
If you reach the bone at the beginning of cauterization, that would be good. If not, then perform cautery again and continue to do so as needed, leaving it for three days. Afterwards, place a cotton swab dipped in butter on top of the eye, and treat the inflammation with a drying agent until it is healed. If 40 days have passed and it is still not healed, then apply a corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and proceed according to what comes in its chapter (i.e. continue treatment as necessary).
And there is a kind of fire cautery for abscesses that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "abscess," and open the place; then put in the incision a thin probe of such a form as this: and they make it to the size of a thumb's width; and hold your hand firmly on the probe, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and it is necessary to put a wet cotton swab dipped in egg white or rose water on the patient's eye: the lead will draw out the pus from the abscess, and the healthy flesh will heal miraculously.
And if the abscess is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer a puncture to the pus and bring the abscess back to the body of the pus according to what is appropriate in its own specific place.

When you treat these cracks, as we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small scalpel-shaped cautery according to this form:

on the abscess of the throat[Note: In this context, "goule" refers to the neck or throat region.]
When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the eye, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and after it becomes rotten and corrupt and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help: then you must use a cautery based on the size of the fistula. After that, place a probe or opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and in its depths; and do this once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in cures, until it heals; and if it is treated in this way, it is good. But if not, then you must uncover the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
from movement of the teeth
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but it does not work, then place the head of the patient in your lap; after that, heat up the cautery until it forms a certain shape as described later, placing a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cauterization as you wish; after that, have the patient fill his mouth with salty water, and gargle for an hour and spit it out.
And in this way, the moving tooth is strengthened and the softened gum is constricted, and the moisture is dried up and spoiled.
of toothache
When toothache is caused by cold or there is cold in the area and medical treatments do not work, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: with butter and with fire.[ISTHMUS OF KOUFRA
Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the end in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and moisten it in boiled butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the virtue of the butter reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and put it on the painful tooth, and put a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which the shape will come after this, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be eased on that same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in anticipation of this cautery, and then spits it out; and this is the shape of the cautery:
When the scrofulous swellings are due to phlegm and cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-cautery with a substance whose form comes after, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery according to its quantity, and leave it like that for three days; and place a wet cotton soaked in butter on the burn until the burn is healed; after that, cure the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.

the healing by fire with iron/metal

of the corn(s) that come to the feet
Very often, a disease arises in the feet, which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large swelling that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this disease is of two kinds: namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is as follows: heat a cauterizing iron as thin as a pen nib, made of good metal, so that it can touch the swelling on all sides, with fine edges; then place it very hot on the swelling, and keep your hand turned tightly around the swelling until it reaches the base of the swelling; and leave it in place for three days until it begins to putrefy; then apply a plaster made of crushed mallow with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the swelling will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound with a cleansing ointment until it is healed.
And if they are converted by moisture in the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in the following way: take a rod of iron or copper, or a pen nib, and place the clot or althelul (that is, powdered verrucae) on the clot; then place the rod on top so that it heats up all around, then add some hot water, and hold your hand tightly, pressing down while turning so that the edges of the rod come into contact with the root of the clot, and can find a path through to the root; and allow the patient to endure the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it in place, and it will detach all by itself along with its roots. Do this repeatedly until you have cauterized all of those on the body, then cure the wounds with ointments that produce flesh.
The treatment for tremors.
When someone trembles from cold nerves or quartan fever or another cause, you should apply four or five cauteries to the spine, one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the chest, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
of stinking pustules
Sometimes, abnormal swellings or stinking pustules that come from corrupted matter appear on the body. In such cases, it is necessary to perform cauterization on each pustule's head as soon as they appear using a fine cauterizing iron made from myrtle wood, with the tip heated in fire, or a long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cauterizing iron. At times, these pustules are cauterized at the beginning in this manner, and they cannot grow any further; instead, the excess matter that causes them is ruptured and healed. However, it is important that this be done after bloodletting.
when an artery is cut[translate.google.com](https://translate.google.com) It often happens that there is a large flow of blood from an artery that is cut in the wound or incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things. And it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
And yet, when this happens to someone, you should quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press down very hard so that the blood is calmed down under your finger and no more drips out; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both small and large, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, depending on the wound and the location where the artery is cut, to the vein where you have placed your finger and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another one quickly from the fire.
And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and take care not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is through one of the four ways we have mentioned: through cautery, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held firmly.
Whoever will manage the stopping of the bleeding by tightly binding it with bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it.[Reference(s):
And if it happens to someone and they do not have any remedy or medicine, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it stops bleeding above the wound and above the vein; and they should not move it, but apply cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations in advance for what they need of cauteries and medicines.[Reference(s):
We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and have described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on head injuries at the beginning up to the feet, and in this chapter I will follow the same path so that one can more easily find what one desires.
And so, as I begin this, it is important for you to know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
And I warn you not to undertake foolish things. For many types of people come to be treated, some of whom are so afflicted by their illness that they easily die from the violence they find in their disease and the severity of their suffering; and one should fear for such people.  [](Note: The text contains several spelling variations and archaic forms that do not affect the meaning.) And of these, there are some who claim to be healed and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the disease is deceitful. It is not at all appropriate to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not rashly but skillfully open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you establish a good reputation, and glory, and lasting praise.
Dear son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.

a swollen head filled with water.
Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the womb grasps the child's head too forcefully; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason that we know of.
And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death hastened; and therefore it seems to me that it is better for me to leave off working on such cures.

After the incision, remove all the moisture; after removing it, bind the incisions with cloth and powder, and put vinegar and oil on it, and leave it like that until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and continue to bind the head as well, and give the patient dry food without much moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.

of rupture/injury

tears
When the tears come from the veins that are above the forehead and no medical treatment helps, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsating sensation on the forehead like a shiver; and if the eyelids are closed and moist such that the paper has fallen off, and the paper is heated up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is necessary.
And this remedy was called "cure contuse" by the ancients, and it consists of shaving the hair from the forehead of the patient who has this illness, then making three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to the length of the forehead. One of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, going down to the eyebrows, while the other two are at the temples above the eyelids. Be careful not to cut the arteries that are located near the temples, and keep your hand away from the jaw bones. Each wound should be the length of three fingers joined together.[ST1]

of the stoppage of the ears
All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or animals, or minerals such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
When something falls into the ear, such as a stone or other object that does not adhere to or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then facilitate extraction; and make them sneeze using a condiment, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward. Often, this cure will cause it to come out; and if it does not come out, facilitate extraction using delicate pincers, of which this is the form:
If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a fine hook made of thin wire; and if it does not come out this way, make a tin tube and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that no air can enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, as often it will come out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take glue (such as used to catch birds) and place some on an instrument made for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out. And if it does not come out with any of the things we have mentioned, then quickly make an incision in the ear so that pus and hardened matter come out, and spasms; and the manner of making the incision is as follows: first make the patient bleed from the head by opening a vein and extracting blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands with their ear facing upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear in the fatty tissue or where it is swollen; and let the incision be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck out the pus with your mouth; treat it until it heals. Of hail or a hailstone. The term "gresle" in Old French can refer to a hailstone or hail in general. It is a natural weather phenomenon where ice pellets or stones fall from the sky during a storm, often causing damage to crops, buildings, and animals.
Many times there come to the paper of the eyes certain things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "gravel" (or "hail"), and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: observe whether the gravel moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision on each side, then gently peel back the skin on both sides, then take it with forceps, and cut it. If you cannot cover it without puncturing the paper a little, do not worry about causing harm to the patient; and if the tear is large, stitch it together, and care for it until it heals; and if it is small, do nothing at all, because the ointments quickly restore it and help the flesh.
And if the gravel is descending inside the ear toward the upper part, then turn over the paper (skin) and extend the gravel with forceps, and cut it and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, do not worry about it; and when the gravel is cut out, rinse the eye with salty water, and cure the wound of what harms the flesh until the patient is healed.

The hairs (or fibers) of paper.
When paper hairs (or fibers) other than those that are natural grow and become ingrown, they harm the eyes and cause various illnesses such as excessive tearing and swelling of the eyelids and cataracts, to the point of causing eye destruction. And there are four ways to cure it: either with a cautery made of fire, or with medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cautery, and this can be done through incision and suturing or by applying bandages, depending on what I will say.
You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle with a thread on it; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow near the hairs, and pull the thread over the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, to the full extent, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then lay on the paper a figure of a pin, such as a myrtle leaf, and nonetheless it is necessary that the figure corresponds to the height that you wish to raise the paper which is divided to all.
And if there is a need to cut a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make an incision to the full extent along the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the large tear duct down to the small one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs, as thick as a root, then insert the probe into one of the two angles of the eye, and scrape it all; then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a needle with a single thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the superfluity of the threads dry on the eyebrows with some sticky substances, if you wish to do so; and if not, then pay no attention, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without drying or constraining things, as the paper will swell at the healing of the wound and bring it together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients have said), and this work is done without fear.

And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the wound become embedded: in this case, you should do as we have said about incisions, but stitches in one and the other are more refined.
The treatment of ulcers is as follows: you should turn the skin and make two incisions in the manner that I have said, and then make two subtle sutures as long as the skin and as wide as the space between them; and cut off the two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; then bring the two ends together gently over the upper part of the skin of the eye, and pull the two sutures tightly from both sides; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin that has been pulled will die and become necrotic and rot until it falls off by itself.

of the eye's decay.
When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or decay occurs in the eye, it can happen in two ways: one naturally, and the other unnaturally. It can suddenly occur due to a wound, a cut, or a cautery, and similar things.
And the method of the treatment is that you split that suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying and constricting substances in the cure of it. Because if you do so, the illness will return worse than before; but use soothing substances, such as fenugreek; and let water agar or althea and flaxseed be cooked, and let heated oils of diaculon be poured into one of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and cure it with this.
And the treasure of your cure is to take heed that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and these treatments that we have mentioned are nothing but corrections for this illness, so that it does not return to the shape that it was before.

of the toe of the eye
Know that the toe (ungle) comes in two forms: it is either nervous and similar to a hard callus, or not nervous but rather resembles congealed white mucus. When one touches it with iron and attempts to pinch it, nothing can be done; and one form or the other begins near the large tear duct (grant larmier) and grows little by little until it covers the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your lap, then you open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand and use tweezers to pull the toe (ungle) upwards; stretch it over a small piece of leather and place it on top. Then take a needle, put a horsehair, cow hair, or buffalo hair through it along with strong thread, bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the toe. Pass the entire needle through and tie the toe with thread, stretching it over the leather. Then skin the side of the toe that follows the vein and artery (prunele) down to the bulb (soie) of the hair, all the way to the head, leaving only the cartilage or tear duct intact so that tears do not flow through the incision as usual. Sometimes the toe is stretched to the bone (oncine) with thread, as we have said; then one skins it gently, removing all of the thin membrane (spatumile), which looks like this:
And be careful that the thin membrane (spatumile) does not touch the fleshy cloth and break, and that the vein (prunele) is not pierced; after the incision, put a little bit of crushed salt and collyrium made from litharge into the eye and leave it until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this similar condition of a nail is often cured with medical methods; and they come to be like I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye look and take the spatula smoothly, not too sharp, according to this form:
And carefully file the nail, and if you see that it is becoming thinner and the swelling approaches, distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red lead and oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then lactate it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid night in the eye causes great harm, then suspend it with a suture and remove a part of it but not all, so that there is no flow of tears; then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Sometimes a red flesh grows over the pupil in some men's eyes, covering the pupil and turning it upwards, appearing like a baluster rose; and the procedure is that the patient puts his head into your hands, then you open their eyes, and remove all that flesh with suitable tweezers, holding it firmly; then cut the first layer of flesh, continuing to cut until the end, making sure not to wound the eye in the process; and let the incision be made with a spatula as we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and small forceps used to remove splinters, as shown in the following form in this chapter.
And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then apply a mixture of rose oil or you can distillate collyrium red and similar corrosive medicines to the eye; place cotton with egg white on the eye outside so that it is secured from hot abscess; if anything remains, and pus accumulates and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with calming agents; then return to your work until the eye has healed, and do this each time flesh grows back in the eye in such a manner.
However, it is necessary to lighten the treatment for each weak eye of natural disposition; and in case of accidental disposition, through iron work; and do not insert your hand into any of these procedures until you see that this limb can withstand the procedure.
of the veins of the eyes
There are red veins that are covered over the eye and take away from its function, weakening the eye all days. Therefore, it is necessary first to look at the eye and see if there is only sebel (a type of inflammation), and not another illness; then, treat the eye in this way: command the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently pull those veins to the very end according to your judgment, and let the pulling be subtle double in this form.
And let there be two strings/ligaments in one piece following this form:
Then, carefully pull those veins with force, and wipe the blood away hour by hour, until you see that the veins move outside of the eye; and take care not to poke the eye with the tips of the spatulas (medical instruments), and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as not to miss those veins; and once you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to dissolve what remains of the sebel.
And if you do not have the power to collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster (medical dressing) for the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and is certain of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method which is before until it heals; and this is the form of the treatment.
of the fistula of the eye
The experts call "arissati" a fistula: when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it that you should lance on the abscess, where it should burst, and drain all the pus in it, until the bone is exposed.
And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then use all the instruments described in the following form; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron with one sharp end, and pointed like a file as in this form:
And place the iron on the corrupt bone, then turn it between your hands and press lightly until you feel that the corruption has been removed; and do this several times, then apply drying medicines.
If the place is healed and flesh has grown, and the wound of the bow is closed, and remains so for 40 days without being renewed or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, then know that it is healed; if not, there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: which is to uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with hot medicine, and when it is exposed, take a gimlet of this form, and let the iron be in three angles, and the rod be tapered up to the end as you see here:
then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye by about a finger width, then turn the entire stylet until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of breathing if they hold their hand on their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened, the matter will go to the nose; this makes it an easier task for the patient.
of the eye socket.
When the eye is open wide all around and there is no discharge or decrease in size, then bind the patient; then clean it, then apply suction cups or a haterel without striking, then place a bandage made of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye, and then compress the eye and dress it with linen bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount of material needed for the eye; then bind it tightly with a strong bandage, and reapply the suction cups without striking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the bandage softens, tighten it again; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good; if not, reapply the dressing and cloths and bandage until it heals.
of the rupture of a round loaf of bread.
When disruptions come to the outer coat (pupil), then it opens, and comes out like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see; if you see such a thing, the procedure is as follows: insert a needle to the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the eyelid; and make it pass through, leaving the first needle in place according to its position; then cut the loose end of the doubled thread and tie one part of the eye around, and bind it tightly, then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth soaked in egg white on top; and leave it until the film sticks to the eye, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is bandaged with a cloth strip all around the eye until it heals.
And if the eye has a great appearance (swelling), then pierce it with a fine stylet that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor flow out and make the eye descend, and enter quickly; then remove it until it heals.
of the eyebow
This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a swelling gathered in the eye, appearing like water descending, and it is not water; and one of the ways to recognize this condition is as follows: have the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then hold their head with both hands, and move it so that you see the swelling come above your eyes; then insert (a probe) and let the light not descend or fall, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not go down, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not arranged as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine stylet and press on the cornea through the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling goes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or boiled water with fenugreek and honey, into the eye; and let it be cured with another cure until it is healed.
of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
We have similar cases of waters (or fluids) in division, and what is necessary to pierce through; and we work accordingly, depending on the health (of the eye). It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light by the sun, and hold the healthy eye very tightly shut; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the tip of the instrument named "almagda" next to the crown by the thickness of a hair in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument named "almagda" strongly, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel when almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is to the depth of the measure from the pupil to the end of the darkness (or color); and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horned canvas, and then put the instrument until it reaches where the water is, and then press it under a path after another. If the water comes out now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.
After a short rest, and if the water rises again along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and no longer rises, gently remove almagda by turning your hand slowly; then put in a little bit of gemstone salt, and raise the eye inside. Then place over it cotton or damp wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye. We (I), and those who are of our time, place common bread broth with plenty of egg.
And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
And then perforate the joint only, and do not go too deep, but make a shallow incision, then apply cautery, as we have said; and at the completion of the procedure, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which they sleep on their back in a dark room; and be devoid of all movements, and partake light meals, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate to perform this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
If abscesses come to a head, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed down, then unbind the vision and place on his face one bandage to cover for some days, and always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house a little at a time, and gradually return to your usual activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.

of the flesh from (off) the nose
Sometimes diverse fleshy growths appear on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are those that have a swelling of fox-colored flesh, while others have soft flesh of good color. In the case of this type of flesh that is soft and not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils and apply the lancet to those growths and pull them out; then cut what you can hold onto with a sharp spatula on one side, until you are certain that all of the flesh is removed.
And if any part remains that cannot be cut, open it with a very sharp and light instrument so that nothing is left; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, cauterize them quickly to stop the bleeding and remove all of the flesh; then pour vinegar or warm water on the nose.
If the nose does not open and moisture reaches the palate, you should know that it is healed; but if the moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is new flesh grown in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut. In this case, you should insert a moderately thick linen thread and tie it with your hands so that there is a space of about one digit between each knot; then place the thread in the patient's nose as far as possible and pull it out while sniffing until it comes through the nose into the mouth. Children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing to do. Then hold the part that comes through the nose with one hand and the part that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and feel your way along the knots in the thread. Do this until you are certain that the knots have rotted the flesh; then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all of the remaining flesh; and then place a piece of linen cloth in the nose for several days until it is healed. If it is necessary to use drying medicines, do so. This is the form of the instrument used to cleanse the head, as oil and medicine are distilled into the nose.
And it is made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, such as a candle, and its conduit is similar; and if you wish, make a closed canal, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
of flesh from the nose
Often, a disease arises in the head of the nose that is called "telul," and it grows and becomes large to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you must lance it at the beginning and remove all of it, then place the cautery or heated medicine on top; and if you delay lancing it until it has become large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, with poor sensation: do not touch it at all with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is lanced even once, great harm can come to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that you can completely lance it, then empty the patient and perform the lancing without fear, and cure the area with drying and constricting substances.
when the nose is lanced and sutured[ ](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/quant%20li%20neis%20est%20copez%20et%20cosus)
Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. The manner of the suture is that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
abscesses of the lips
To some men, hard abscesses like peas, smaller and larger, appear within the lips. Then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each lump, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply the place after the incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped; and then leave it open to air, and cure the place of dry things until it heals.
of the flesh of the gums
Often, a swollen flesh arises on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with forceps and cut its root, and let the pus or blood run; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
of deafness.
Sometimes, hard and rough shells gather at the base of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, which are unsightly; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, and greenish, such that corruption reaches the gum, causing bad breath; it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and clean the teeth or shells until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what comes out at the first scraping, that is good; otherwise, repeat the process on the second and third day, until everything is removed; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments to be cleaned, depending on what the work requires, because the rasps used to clean outside the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; and have these forms and others prepared.
When you cure teeth, it is necessary to delay pulling them as much as possible, because this should not be done hastily; for it is a very important substance until there is no excuse for scraping (or removing the tooth). Then when the patient is ready to pull, you should make sure of the decayed tooth. Often it happens that the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not leave, because the abscess remains, as we have often seen with surgeons. And when you are certain of the decayed tooth, you should cauterize all around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum on all sides; then pull it with your hands or with delicate tweezers firmly at first and then more gently, until it is well loosened; then securely fasten the tweezers; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is cracked and decayed, you must fill it with pieces of cloth where the cracks are; and carefully fasten it with tweezers so that it does not break when tightening; and one must work very delicately around the gum to loosen the tooth.
And be careful that you do not break it and leave a part in, which would cause greater pain for the patient due to the malice of the root. Be careful not to act as ignorant surgeons sometimes do, who out of haste and recklessness sometimes break the jawbone and do not provide what is needed; but instead bring about great sickness from the remaining roots or from the broken jawbone, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, or salt water; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.

When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is not erupted in a straight position, and it cannot be pulled or filed: then remove it; but if it is loose with the other tooth, take this instrument, the shape of which is shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
