when the tooth falls out.
When the teeth loosen in front, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success, then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth (if there are one or more) between the loose teeth, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from the part where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers, align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, so that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it tightly in place as long as it can endure, and if it loosens or the wire breaks, then constrict it with another wire; if it remains in place, it will serve thus all its time, and this is the method for aligning teeth and realigning two loose teeth, as you see.
And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place immediately, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled interfere, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
to cut the wire of the tongue.
Sometimes there is a ligament under the tongue that is natural and present at birth, or it can occur due to an accident of a healed wound. The procedure is as follows: you open the patient's mouth, have their head in your lap, and lift the tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment. If there is hardness or knot, it is due to the healing of a wound, then use a hook and cut the ligament widely. Be careful not to cut too deep, as the artery is located beneath it. Once you have finished, apply warm rose water and eau de laxative or cold water under the tongue, then place a linen tent under the tongue. The patient should wear this every night so that the wound does not heal. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol and if it continues to bleed, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this. Then continue treatment until it heals.
And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then throw the "oncine" on it, and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood overcomes your work, then put vinegar powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the limb gently and leave it to be healed, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
of abscesses in the throat
Sometimes there come within the throat growths that are called "godath," and they are properly referred to as "the two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be cautious: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and bluish color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it at all with iron, for fear of bleeding; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will break on its own; and if it is of a white color and has fine roots, then have your instruments ready to cover, but first look to see if the hard swelling is at rest and calm. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and let his chin be in your lap, and have the servant open the mouth and take the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue down beneath the entire instrument, of which this is the method; and it should be of silver or fine brass, just like a knife:
And press the tongue down beneath this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the "oncine" and insert it into the almond, and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, of which this is the method, which resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are curved towards each other, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or steel:
And if you do not have this tool at hand, then take pliers, of which this is the form:
And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner; and after the incision, rinse the patient's throat with warm water, and water and vinegar, and if bleeding occurs, rinse the patient's throat with water, or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them then in the same way as the two almonds.
And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely one of small size; and it had completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was stopped up, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for one day or two. And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two pieces through the two nostrils. I therefore acted quickly and inserted a probe into one of them; then I pulled it out and drained a large amount of pus; then I did the same thing in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut off a piece of it, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled the space that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I squeezed it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it no longer grew; and I left those parts without knowing what God did with her after me.
of the grape (from Latin "uva") or from Old French "ueil, oeil" meaning egg. Without more context, it is difficult to determine which one is intended in this case.
When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye". Once it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is thin, then it is necessary to make an incision; and the one that is round assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a fuscous color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision on it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you must have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and make an incision with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it heals. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a ruse with cauterization without fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp pointed. And it is that the patient places their head on your healthy part, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and apply live steam, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the steam from this instrument, of which this is the shape:
And have a hair on the head where one applies the medicine, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie down on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and cause choking; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour, until you see it reddened and the bites of the medicine have calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with the cotton all the way into the corner above, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to start the cautery of the medicine again, then do so, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with a swab wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it heals.
This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put a spout on it, and boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have an instrument shaped like this: And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the eyes be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes mortified; then restart it often, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and never do it except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to overwhelm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with health.
Often a bone or a fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what you cannot see and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit after the food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come up through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, then take an instrument of plastic of this shape:

of the swelling of the throat

And if the sick person becomes hoarse all day, then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the tonsil feels the water, it will fall out.

The chapter of abscesses.
Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what the memory brings hereafter of one and the other in this book; and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its likeness itself, and those that hold moisture. And the second way is for the locations where they are in the body. For abscesses of the head are different than those of the base, and abscesses of the fleshy part are different than those that come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, by which it causes contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the base, so one should pierce it while it is still alive; and it is not appropriate to pierce a grown abscess without completed digestion, except for those that are near the base, so that it does not rot inside and form a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the incision in the lower part of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and on all sides where there is no cavity.
And in those that swell, according to the member. And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better to leave the incision until it is firm in completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body of it will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member requires. And in small abscesses, make small incisions; and in large abscesses, make large incisions, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where you must sew the core and cover it; when it has become as a piece of cloth, and is dead, it is necessary to do as one does with boils; and some abscesses are cut in three angles, and some have cuts like the leaf of myrtle, such as angina abscesses; and there are those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce it; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, do not pull out all the pus in that hour, but pull out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then pull out something more; do this many times, bit by bit, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak virtue, such as women, small children, old and decrepit men. For the spirit sometimes jumps when the pus comes out, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not notice. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe away the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, then apply linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many holes, then it is necessary to put in a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of the skin in the abscess and turned it over, then it is necessary to fill it with old linen cloth or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it heals.
And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold and clear water, and moisten a cloth, and place it on the bleeding site multiple times. And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, lightly applied. And if this is in winter, and the location where the abscess is is very sensitive, then you must put tents and wet cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is in summer, and the location is fleshy, then you must place damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said. And then loosen the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as necessary, until it heals.
And this is what must be generally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is this chapter.
"des soros" likely refers to "abscesses" or "swellings." The term comes from Latin "sors," meaning a lot or drawing of lots. In medical contexts, it referred to the pus-filled swelling that forms when a part of the body is infected.
Where small abscesses of the head come, and they are of two kinds, as the joints of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty and such where there is moisture like pustules; and some are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not contradict. And the work of cutting consists of trying every one instrument that is called "entromissoire", of which the form comes after, what thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, so you pierce above the long [one]. And when the moisture has been drained, so skin without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again if anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will cure this. And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you are sure that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound with suitable ointment, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds a hard core, so cut it lengthwise; and throw your sutures there, and skin it all around, and put all your effort into drawing out the cyst where it lies; and if the artery contradicts you, so do what I told you after. And similarly do for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure as I told you.
And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And some of these abscesses on the head or where there is no moisture, and one of those abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and found the abscess as a hard, rough and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had struck it, they would have made as much wound as with a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those that come to children's heads and roots of ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that pus can exit easily; and cure them as is necessary.
The term "scrophules" refers to a type of abscess or swelling that was commonly found in the lymph nodes of the neck. In medieval medical texts, scrophules were often associated with tuberculosis and other chronic infectious diseases. Treatment for scrophules typically involved surgery to drain the pus and abscesses, as well as the use of various ointments, salves, and other remedies to promote healing and prevent infection. The term "scrofula" is derived from the Latin word "scrofa," meaning "female pig," possibly because the swollen lymph nodes resembled the swelling of a pig's neck glands.
Scrophules often occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in other areas of the body, and are connected to each other. Each scrofula is specifically located within its own cavity, as we have described with neck abscesses and head abscesses. The similarities of these scrophules are many. Some contain moisture, while others are malignant and do not want to obey health. In that one you see with good disposition, and has the color of the skin, and moves easily from each side, and is not swollen in the nerves of the neck or in the artery or conduit, and is not deep; so it should be cut open from above, and skinned on all sides, and pull the two lips of the wound with sutures if necessary, as we have said about head abscesses; and drain the pus bit by bit, and make sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and the scalpel should not be sharp or cutting, so that little is left behind, and does not go too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder or any drying powders in the wound, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skill if there remain any small scrofulous lumps, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, do not cut this scrofula at its root, but bind it with a double strong thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then bandage it.
And if you cut the entire scrofula, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it up, making sure there is no excess flesh due to the size of the scrofula. You must focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sew it as we have said. For those scrofulas that have excess flesh, pierce them where it appears necessary; and pierce them as described earlier, by hanging, then apply dressings with oil and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a healing ointment until it heals.

of the chancre
We have mentioned in the division the similarities of chancre and how it should be treated with medicines and how to avoid iron treatment. And we say that chancre worsens in the marrow, and great caution is required in its treatment. The ancients said that when chancres are in a place where they can be scraped, such as chancres on breasts, thighs, and similar places, it should all be removed when it first appears. And when it has grown and become old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never healed any from it; nor did anyone heal it before me.
The procedure, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have mentioned, is to first purge the patient of black bile once; then make them sweat if they show clear signs of indigestion. Then prepare the patient for the procedure by providing a comfortable place for them. Next, throw your instruments onto the chancre and remove all hair from around it without leaving any behind. Let the blood flow freely and press the area with your hand or some object until bleeding stops completely. If the natural course of bleeding is contrary to incisions on the artery or vein, cauterize the area until the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with other remedies until it heals completely.

"of the surgical incision on the abscess" or "of the cutting open of the abscess" The event of this branch (of the arteriae iliaca) is due to the section that comes from the syphac (the abscess in the groin), or the extension on the stomach in the side of the haunches, due to which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the hips.

And the signs when it is from the extension of the abscess are that it happens frequently, over a long period of time, and not suddenly. And the abscess is even (swollen) all the way down to its depth because the syphac presses on the intestines.
And the sign is when it is of the syphilis section, that it brings about at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscesses are diverse apparent, under the skin close by, and this is due to the evacuation of the intestine and flesh through the syphilis's defect.
And sometimes the membranes (cirbes) come out with the intestines and are retained inside, causing great pain to the patient, even when they are pressed.
And in these iron treatments, there is reason to fear, so one must be cautious.
And the method of this treatment is that you instruct the patient to use their hand to draw the intestines back into the wound, if they can reinsert it. and then have them lean on their neck between your hands, while lifting their thighs;
then stretch out the back and cut all the skin of the hips lengthwise; then insert into the flanks hooks according to what you need for opening the wound, and make them long enough for the intestines to exit;
then flay the suet that is beneath the hip skin until all of the white suet is exposed;[In this context, "syfac" refers to a layer of fatty tissue located directly under the skin. and separate the area that is behind the anus, and move your hand to the right into the cavity of the hips. then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads and insert it into the back part of the abscess, which is behind the skin of the groin; after the spine, cut the ends of the visible threads until there are four threads left. then arrange the threads in the shape of a cross and tie the abscess, which is under the skin of the groin, with a strong ligature made of two strands; then wrap the ends of the threads and tie them firmly with two strands so that no vessels can enter the wound and cause an abscess. and place again the ligament according to the first long ligament two fingers' width away from it, and after these two ligaments leave the suture which is below the heart of the hips one digit wide.

of the softening of the skin of the buttocks
The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the fat inside is liquefied and it is visible; and when one wants to cure it, it is necessary to make the patient lie on their stomach, and then cut the softened skin on the natural skin; then bring the two lips together with a suture, and if you see, first sew up the excess of softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds until it is healed and the thread falls out.
Of castration.
Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is so that the physician knows how to answer when asked about it and how to cure it; and the other because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and other beasts. So I say that castration is done in two ways: either by attrition or by cutting. In the one we do by attrition, we make the animal sit in hot water until the genitals are softened and hanging; then pull them with your hand until they retract and you no longer feel them. Regarding castration by cutting: it is necessary to tie up the animal, and press the skin of the genitals with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each testicle once, when you have well skinned them; and leave some of the soft tissue and fine tissue that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is better than the one done by attrition because in attrition there may be a remnant of the genitals left, due to which the animal still desires lust; then cure the wound until it heals.
of hermaphrodites
Hermaphrodites are of two kinds for men: one is when between the two hips there is an opening as in the shape of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes urine flows. And the other kind is for women, with a bulge like a man's virile member and two hips. And the treatment for both sexes is to cut away the fused parts and cure them like other wounds. In the second kind of men, when urine shoots through the skin of the hips, there is no cure.
"tentigine" does not appear in the given text. It is possible that it was a typo and the correct term is "tetigene", which means "that which can be touched or felt". However, without more context, it's difficult to provide an accurate translation.
Tentigene is a growth that attaches to the natural parts, and it is too unsightly to see; some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment: You must bind the excess of the tentigine to your hand or with bandages, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, for fear of causing bleeding. After curing one wound, move on to another growth that arises at the mouth of the marris (possibly a type of skin lesion), and use it, and perhaps it will heal on its own, and it resembles a cow's udder, and because of this, it was called by the ancients "cow disease." It must be cut in the same way as we have said for tentigine, and cured until it is healed.
of something erratic or prone to dislocation
An erratic condition exists when the nature of a woman is not functioning properly, or the opening is small; this can be natural at birth or caused by disease; or it may result from a tight ligature, or subtle and fine syphilis, which has penetrated deep into the matrix, on the sides, below, or elsewhere. This prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes even menstruation. The recognition of this condition is through the observation of the belly. If the obstruction is visible, then use your fingers or a probe. If it is subtle syphilis and located near the two lips, then act quickly: place your two index fingers together, with the woman lying on her back, legs spread apart; then stretch the two lips widely apart, so that the subtle syphilis is exposed and lies over the obstruction. Then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on top of the obstruction. The woman should have sexual intercourse every day, so that it does not heal. If the syphilis is hard and thick, then use a spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf. If the obstruction is made of thick flesh, then suspend it with a needle and cut it; and use hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then insert a wide horn or tube so that the wound does not heal; this should be done for a long time, until it is cured. If flesh has grown in the matrix, then cut it according to this method, unless there are large abscesses. For an enlarged abscess in the matrix, do not touch it with any instrument.
of hemorrhoids: "des" is a contraction of "de les", meaning "of the", and "emorroides" refers to swollen veins in the rectum or anus.
Hemorrhoids are enlarged veins that are not usually visible but become so over time, and when they become old, they turn into a type of growth called "thelul". We have already discussed the similarities and signs of hemorrhoids earlier, and now I will mention those that can be treated. Hemorrhoids and "thelul" that are inside the rectum or anus and not visible to touch cannot be cured with surgery. Those that are at the opening of the rectum can be felt and therefore cured. It is necessary to place the woman in a cool room, then use pincers to pull out the hemorrhoids by their roots, then apply powdered medicines that constrict blood flow, such as acacia and dragon's blood, and similar things. Then let her stand with her back against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water. If bleeding occurs, place her in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peel, galls, and similar things. Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg yolk, and make a plaster to apply on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, then apply cups to the back and breasts without breaking the skin; then take wool, moisten it in plantain or cleaver juice with old wine, and heat it on the area. Once the swelling has subsided, cure the wound with ointment until it heals. The one called "albathir" is red and looks like a rough surface, it should be treated as mentioned for hemorrhoids and cured until it heals.
of abscesses on the groin
Many types of abscesses occur in the groin, such as chancre, abscesses filled with pus, herpes, ecthyma, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, as well as other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that burst on their own; and if you wish to know about the operation with fire, look and see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if you can see it. Then, do not rush to pierce, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and place two small seats where they can lean back, and support their back and stretch out their legs past the thigh; and let their hips be spread apart, and place their arms beneath their knees, and bind them well with a good ligament; then turn them towards the right side, and prepare the instrument used to open the groin, which will be described later; and it is necessary that when you wish to prepare this instrument, you insert the rod first to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary for him to place the funnel of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens and is emptied by hand, it should be covered with a clean cloth or sponge; and when the pus has drained, place wet compresses in oil of roses or dry olive oil in the wound; and place the compress deep within the groin, and then place a clean linen cloth moistened with water or malvasia wine on top of the groin and the bandage; then dress the wound after two days with an appropriate ointment until it is healed; and sometimes the groin and wound are cleaned out with an enema of water and honey, and then boiled lily roots and aristolochia longa are added; then return to dressing the wound. And if the wound is healing in the groin, be careful not to use hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
of childbirth
It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural shape of childbirth and its signs, which are: when you see the woman press downwards and have a desire to smell something, then know that this birth is in accordance with nature, and the baby's position is under its head, and the afterbirth is with it; and when you see these signs, gently press on her stomach so that the baby comes out quickly, for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the groin is cleaned of its impurities through good cleansing; but if it comes any other way, then it is not natural. For sometimes it comes with its feet first, or comes outside the body, such as the legs or arms, or it comes on its stomach, or turns over onto its neck, and may take on other bad positions. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these matters, and to be wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes and how one should help in each case.
If the child comes out of the womb headfirst, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a seat, or have women hold her; and anoint her vagina with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then insert for her the small speculum of the following form: and split the membrane, and cut the child's nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and support the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give the woman an enema of powdered fenugreek with oil of cumin; then make her drink a strong-smelling substance and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: the child will come out now. And if the two hands emerge outside, then you must gently straighten them one after the other; and if they cannot enter, then make the woman sit on a seat with her feet raised up; then lower the seat to the ground and support the woman so that she does not fall during the procedure; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut the child's hands with the knife that is placed here in front, and extract the child, and straighten it out as well.

Of arrows
Arrows are diverse in their appearances and in the parts of the body where they land.
The diversity of arrows is such that there are some with large points, small ones, feathered and unfeathered, and some with blunt tips. and some have two wings or barbs, some have tongues, and others are split or cleft.[*I translated "lengues" as "tongues" because it was a common term used to refer to the barbs or projections on the tip of an arrow in medieval medical texts. The term "pieces" likely refers to the pieces or fragments that can be left in the wound when the arrowhead breaks off during extraction.*] And when an arrow falls into a limb, it does so in two ways: either it strikes the principal member and
like brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members. When it dislocates in any part of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you appear: then you must be careful with the extraction of this arrow, for death often follows in many ways; and when you do not see those bad signs and the arrow is not deep, then extract it and treat the wound.[5](Note 1)

Here begins the book of fractures.[IBM Watson]{.underline}
This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it concerns the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Know, dear son, that foolish doctors who ignore this chapter have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read any letters (i.e., they are uneducated and ignorant of medical knowledge).
And for this reason, the practice of medicine is strange in our land because I have never found a single good one (i.e., a competent doctor).[/3.
And I know nothing except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have mastered the subject, and through experience and habituation from my life.
And I have described in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in these two chapters before.
Then it is necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summary of the meaning and the chapters where the wise man directs his attention, and remains on the truth, so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruise comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one side and the other, if no obstacle prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, or the elderly.
Or if the weather is not extremely hot or too cold, and he avoids cold things, that is, cold battles, and bird and hare meat, and does not drink wine, nor eats fatty meats, and does not fill himself with food which fills the veins with blood, until you are certain there is no danger of a hot abscess or spreading matter to the limb; then let the patient return to their usual regimen that they were following before.
And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide good nutrition and viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, meat from the head, feet, and entrails of animals, eggs, fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things. For at times, with some setting, muscles and tendons appear sooner and heal more quickly.

of the different ways of fracture There are many types of fractures, with various shapes, and different causes;
for there are fractures made by the impact of a sword, and the collar bone takes away all the bone down to the symphysis which is under the bone, like that of an axe or stick; and this type of fracture is called "hechure".
Or when the sword hits the bone from above without penetrating it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and this wound can be large or small for these two types of fractures.
And if there is an embedded impact, or a fracture from a stone, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
And if there is a fracture that reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.
And if there is a wound that has penetrated into the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called this type of fracture "hairline" (or "capillary").[Answer revised after rereading the original text. of the shoulder fracture
It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates without being noticed, except through touch; therefore, treat it according to the type of fracture, and reset it in its natural position in every way possible; then place on the area powdered flour with a lot of egg white, and light bandages, and put on a double cloth; then place a wide and thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate in any part of the shoulder, fill those areas with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then bind it firmly with a large bandage so that the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it softens, tighten it again, and adjust the plate if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days has passed, untie it, but be careful, because it is not an easy thing for the bone to come out of place.
And if a piece of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breaking of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.
In the breaking (fracture) of the arm.
The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks near the joint. And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of blood flow, quickly, and perhaps they vomit blood, and the fracture can be seen clearly in the broken bone, and one can tell easily.
And the restoration (treatment) is that the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then you press the shoulders together and bring the ribs of the two sides together with your hands, gently adjusting them equally as much as possible so that the shape of the bone is correct. Then you apply poultices and compresses made of salt or some other light wood over the fracture, and wrap it in a bandage, tying it securely to the broken bone so that it does not move; and tie the bandage around their back, tightening it appropriately, and check frequently to make sure it has not loosened. If it becomes loose due to corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, remove the poultice, and treat what has come there in accordance with medical practices; then reapply the poultice and tighten it until it is healed.
of the breaking of ribs
Know that the breaking of ribs only comes about in heavy blows to the back and the chest, and they do not bend further because they are slippery; and this can be easily detected by examining the wounds.
And the setting of the broken ribs is to align the break as it should be. Then apply a poultice and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
And if the breaking of ribs leans inward, then the patient feels great pain and shortness of breath, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lining; and there is sharp pain in the side, and immediate vomiting of blood, which is a serious condition. of the break of the neck.
Sometimes there comes a break in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back. And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, see if you notice their hands are softened, swollen, and without feeling, and that they cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. You should know that in many cases this means death, but if they can move them and feel well when pressed and poked, then the joints of the bone are safe, and the patient will be healed if treated.
And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, look to see if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms present in the hands, and on the back there is a swelling without desire to be egested; and when it is turned onto its stomach, there is still egestion without desire. And when it is turned onto its back and it wants to move, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor in its care.
And if these symptoms do not occur, the condition is easier to deal with.
The treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess on the spine, apply heated oil of roses or egg yolk until it calms down; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters and bind it with a bandage, ordering the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain until it is healed. And if any bone becomes dislodged, it is necessary to cover the wound with linen; remove the bone and stitch up the two lips of the wound if it is large; apply a healing ointment until it heals. If the head of the bone is broken (called "head of the cow"), insert your left hand into the wound and push the bone back in place as far as you can, then apply a plaster and bandage if necessary. Restrain the area and if there are any dislodged bones, remove them and clean the wound until it heals.
of the fracture of the shin bone
It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight reduction in size at the top; and it bends long, and tilts to the side, and comes to the patient pain and swelling at the site of the break.
And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand over the break, so that you are above the breaker; and know what the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the top, then make the break even, so that it is in its natural shape.
And if the break is long, or it tilts to the inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that break can be prepared for you.[IT] Et se il avient que li os sunt desjoinctz ou par chu de hors ou par chu dedens, si li fai cheoir sus le dos ou sur un baston qui soit a ses piez; et si les remet ensemble dou sovent. And when you have made it even, then apply the poultice, then place a wooden or iron bar on top of it and tighten the breaker so that it does not move; and apply medication under the ribs until the ligaments are aligned.
And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we mentioned before; then return to treatment and bind it as is appropriate, unless there is any adverse event; and this is the method.
on the dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder joint is the one that is between the neck and the arm, and if it is dislocated, it should be treated in one of two ways: the first way is to take a rod of medium thickness, shaped like this:[This sentence contains some instructions for shaping a rod, but I'll need more context or an illustration to accurately translate that part.]
And tie the two ends of the shoulder joint with two ligaments and fasten them upwards, and lay the patient on a seat; then throw their broken arm over the rod until it reaches the armpit and forms a bow shape around the rod; then suspend it from some heavy weight or have the minister stretch it downwards; then place the surgeon's hands together over the break, holding them in that position until the bones return to where they should be.
And the other manner is as follows: lay the patient face down on a support, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants, one of whom should hold what is above the break with his hands, and the other below, at every ligament, and each extend it in its direction.
And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tighten one ligament above and below the break, and have each of the assistants extend it in its direction. And if the break is near the shoulder joint, then you must place one ligament in the middle beneath the armpit, and another towards the side, beneath the break; and do the same if the break is towards the side. Then align the break as it should be, and tighten it if there is no danger of abscesses.
And if an abscess does occur, then do not tighten it for seven days and instead place a linen cloth soaked in vinegar and rose oil on the break until the abscess subsides; then tighten it. The method of tightening is as follows: apply the poultice to the break, then place the arm on a support, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and place the bandage, and tighten it on the arm and the support so that the arm remains in place, unless something prevents it, or if the bones are not aligned.
And if you suspect that the bones are not aligned, then use a device called an "estel," and place above the break a wider and stronger estel than the others, with a space of one finger between each estel, and each estel should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side. Then tighten it over the estels as I described at the beginning of this chapter on the break, first tightly and then less so as you move away.
And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you reset the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine every three days if there is itching, inflammation, or coming of fluid to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. If that is the case, loosen it, as we have said.
And if no such accidents occur, then do not unbind it before three or more days have passed, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool beneath the affected area, and check every hour of the day and night if the shape of the broken member has changed or if the bindings have loosened; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give the patient the food that we mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially light; and when they begin to recover, make it richer. And it is customary for the affected area and leg to be recovered in 40 days in total; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to direct the place. And if the stricture is bad and swollen, then delay unbinding for one day or two months.

of the break of the hand

Of the broken hip
The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is evident when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is to tie one ligature above the fracture, and another below it. And the patient lies on his face, then each of the assistants extends their ligature to their equal part; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
And if the fracture is near the hip's root, let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture. And likewise if it is near the knee, and then let the ligament be next to the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the doctor place the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bandage, if pus does not appear.
And if there is a hot abscess, let it settle down, then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is made in such a way. You should wrap around the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, leaving the excess; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg next to the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come up; then wrap around the leg and the thigh the bandage, then put on the fracture a stylet, and one stylet on the bone of the leg; then apply soft cloths on the gap between the leg and the thigh to make equal the tightening, then begin to tie strongly three or four turns above the fracture; and when it goes above the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and bind them with three stitches that are above, then go down below to the end of the thread, so that you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, if no abscess or swelling or any similar thing appears.

And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and arm; however, with this kind of restoration, the patient is not made completely better.
And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in complexions.
of the groin by the knee.

of the fracture of the arm bone (os du poignet)

And if you wish, take a bladder of a sheep, attach a cane to its opening, insert the entire bladder into her wound; blow strongly into the cane until the bladder is filled inside: the nature (body) will return and the fracture will heal; then fill it with cotton and leave it for several days until it is healed.

of fracture with wound

boils that come on the suture
We often come after the healing of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Take care then if the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, taking one of these things, or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg white or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in cloths, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen, and begin another, until the knot is removed; or you strain on a piece of wood well made; for the property of wood is that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the knot has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess appear; or you have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and thin afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the nutrients could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to large movements at an inopportune time; or because there is little blood in its body, so it is weak.
And the cure is to make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that blood multiplies in him; and administer baths, and give joy and pleasure; then apply a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice draws great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with cold water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and it regains its natural appearance.
of the crooked limb after health(iness)
When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bones are openly broken, and the shape of the member is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land; and these works are to be blamed, and come great harms, and perhaps death; nonetheless, if the nodules and the tension are fresh, then they should be soaked in hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as vismalve leaves, and roots, and mellilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as good diaculum, and take the marrow of vismalve, and cook it with goose fat or oil of St. John's wort, and make a plaster; or take greasy figs, and crush them with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.

And if the twisting is grown old and hardened, as with stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be covered to the bone with a sharp incision, lightly with a delicate lancet; and place cushions and support in the care.
Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocation arises from a joint being out of its place, which prevents movement, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be returned to its proper position immediately.
For if one waits, the area swells and there is a risk that it cannot be put back in place; therefore, one must not move it when it is swollen, as this often results in spasms and other pains.
Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then allow them to rest until the swelling has subsided; then apply hot water and oil to the limb, gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its place.[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trait%C3%A9\_de\_Maitre\_Henri\_de\_Mondeville](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trait%C3%A9_de_Maitre_Henri_de_Mondeville)
And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the joints from the head to the feet.
Of the jaw[s].
It is rare for both jaws to be dislocated, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly displaced from their proper position and become somewhat relaxed, or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, causing saliva to flow out of the mouth that the person cannot hold in or close their mouth, and their tongue becomes entangled as they speak.
When the dislocation is small, it may return to its proper position through various means.[1](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Quant%20li%20dislocations%20est%20petite%2C%20si%20revient%20par%20li%20em%20plusors%20disposicions.)

And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and places the tip of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and let the other hand be free to ensure evenness. And command the patient to relax, move their jaws from side to side.
And the physician keeps it even, until it returns to its place.
And if the returning is difficult, even if it's both jaws together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can gently reset them. Do not delay in resetting, as we have said.[Given context: The text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French around the 12th-13th centuries, providing instructions for various medical procedures, including setting dislocated jaws.]
And when they are evenly reset and the patient's mouth closes properly without difficulty, place wet cloths soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on top. Then bind it gently with soft bandages.[Given context: The text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French around the 12th-13th centuries, providing instructions for various medical procedures, including setting dislocated jaws.]
and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head resting between two cushions, so that it is not moved to the right or left, and do not strain to chew, but eat light food until the pains are eased, and the jawbones are unlocked.
and then let him eat what he wants, lightly, and do not strain to open his mouth while eating or drinking, until the jawbone is fully healed and healthy.

of the fork/fracture/dislocation
The dislocation cannot be removed from the ribcage along its length and from the side, and it is dislocated in such a way that it is noticeable.
And the treatment is as follows: have the patient lie flat on their back, stretch out their arms, and press firmly with your palm on the affected area until it returns to its proper place. It could also be interpreted as "the patient's palm", but that would not make much sense in this context.]
and the head of the shoulder that is dislocated towards the back cannot be repositioned either. If it can at all, then you should reset it to its proper place as we have described. Then apply a poultice and bandage, secure it in place, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed.
And similarly, bring back the head of the shoulder when it has become dislocated from its place.
of the dislocation of the shoulder
Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways only: one of which is when it dislocates at the part of the socket underneath; the second is when it dislocates at the part of the hip; and it may rarely dislocate at the part above, but this happens infrequently.
And it should never dislocate backward at the shoulder blade, nor should it dislocate inward toward the nerves; and often it dislocates downward toward the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for it easily slips out in them; but in those who have sufficient flesh, it hardly ever slips out, and never returns easily.
And it may happen to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, causing their shoulder to swell with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.[ST1] However, the text suggests that in such cases, the problem is actually an abscess rather than a dislocation. The words "percussion" and "casseure" refer to blows or fractures, while "aposteme chaut" means a hot abscess. The text advises against assuming that the shoulder is dislocated simply because it is swollen, as this may not be the correct diagnosis. Instead, the text suggests carefully examining the affected limb and considering other possible causes of the symptoms.
Therefore, you should examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it moves down towards the shoulder blade, and there will be a noticeable difference between the healthy and injured shoulder; And you will find a pit at the top of the shoulder and below the shoulder blade where it touches the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg, and the patient cannot bring their hand to their side nor make any movements.
And similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it will not be concealed, as you can clearly feel it when touching.[ADD\_MORE: ]And if the shoulder dislocation is in front, it is not hidden either because you can see it; and if it is dislocated backwards, it is noticeable when the patient tries to move their arm.
And this type of dislocation is not difficult to set right, when it is new or if the patient is a child.
And the method is for the caregiver to lift the patient's hand up high, then place their own fingers under the shoulder blade and forcefully lift the joint upwards in its proper place; the caregiver should then raise the arm and stretch it out straight, before placing it back down. This will cause the dislocation to quickly return to its normal position.[ADD\_MORE: ]It is important to note that this method of reducing a shoulder dislocation should only be performed by trained medical professionals, as there is a risk of further injury if not done correctly. Also, the patient may experience significant pain and discomfort during the process, but it is necessary for their recovery. After the reduction, the affected arm should be immobilized with a sling or brace to prevent further movement and promote healing. Additionally, the caregiver should monitor the patient closely for any signs of complications, such as swelling, bruising, or difficulty moving the arm, and seek medical attention if necessary.
And if it does not come as we have said in many days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and administer a soothing and softening remedy, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let them be administered.
Then have the patient lean on their back, and place a woolen support underneath the affected side, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the patient's heel on the support, and lift the healthy shoulder upward, and pull the patient's hand.[](https://fr.glosbe.com/fr/en/althea.html)
And let another assistant hold the patient's head so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will immediately return to its place, and if you see it is dislocated in this way, reset it as follows:
and make sure there is a person present who is bigger than the patient; and let them stand to the patient's side, and push their shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and let another assistant pull the patient's hand down towards the stomach. And if the patient is too light, have them hold onto something heavy, and the dislocation will be corrected now.

And it is necessary that the patient eats only soft food until the limb is healed, as this will help it heal more quickly; and then they can eat normally after 5 or 7 days, and begin to move the limb; if it feels firm and is no longer swollen, then it is healed.

of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been put back in place, as it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each figure (shape). And when you join the patient's rib with the healthy (rib), it can be seen clearly. For the joint is misaligned and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder on all sides.
And you must reset it (the rib) in such a way that abscesses come (to form), because if abscesses come, then setting it would be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset at all, especially when it is at the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
And the restoration is, when it is such that it can be reset, that you hold out the patient's hand with your two hands; and let their arms be spread out, and the healer's hands should be around the rib, both above and below, and push the joint together at its ends or at the base of the palm until it returns to its place.
And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the dislocated bone.
And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and let two people extend the arm, and hold it with two cloths so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side after you have wrapped a long and wide bandage around it.
And when the physician has joined the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then strongly pushes the joint until it returns.[ clearsession](user)
And when it is in its place, put dry ointment with egg white on it, and bind it firmly, and raise the arm of the patient to his neck, and leave it for several days, then loosen it.[clearsession](user)
And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the tie and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not bind well, then repeat the ointment and tie, and leave it like this for several days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or put sheep fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath; And when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you wish, put damp cow dung warmed with butter, and bind it on. And it will return to its normal position.
the dislocation of the hand
The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is easy, more so than for other joints; nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place at once when it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen, or there comes a hot abscess.
And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and position the patient's palm to be even with the appearance of the joint, and then apply pressure until it aligns.
Nonetheless, you must verify if it is in the correct position; then, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and realignment. And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table and you place your hand on the appearance of the joint. If it aligns now, then it is good.[ADDITIONAL REQUEST] Here are two more sentences to translate in the same format as before:

And it does not harm the patient as long as their hand remains moist and they cannot grasp anything; then you know that the nerves or arteries are cut, and there is no other means except to constrict with the fire cautery near the wound, and perhaps it will be of no use.
And when the hand is in place, apply the ointment that we mentioned, then bind it up and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
And if he cannot move it well, and there is some cracking sound, moisten it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.[Expand to see the original text] Et s'il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d'aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu'il soit sanez.
on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the stomach;
Then stretch the finger and push the dislocation back into place until it is reset, then hold the base of the finger and bend it towards the side that is dislocated.
And leave it for two days, and then align it properly on that day. Wrap it with a bandage as we have said, and unwrap it during the day, make it move, and re-wrap it at night. Repeat this frequently until it becomes firm.[
And do the same if it is dislocated on the palm side of the hand and proceed in the same way as you have done before until it has healed. And do the same thing when it is dislocated from any other direction.
of the loins in the back
When the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is imminent for the patient.
And the sign is that evacuations will occur involuntarily and cannot be controlled, and often certain limbs will become weakened, or one or both thighs or arms.
And often the back will dislocate in four places; the one that dislocates at the back is called "gilbositez."
The treatment is to determine if "gilbositez" has come from infancy; if so, there is no cure or complete healing.
And if it has come from falling or impact or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment say in grand terms that there is not much benefit in all cases.
but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in diverse ways.
I say that in the swelling (gillen-bosity) that comes to the breast beforehand, there is no remedy or cure.
and also that which comes directly in the two ribs, it cannot be cured unless it is the one that comes to the back, as I am saying.
and it is necessary that the patient be lying on their back with their body evenly positioned, and have something to support them underneath so they do not get injured.
Then insert a stake into the ground at the head and another one at the feet, and tie a rope under the patient's armpits, and another around their thighs, knees, and ankles.
and two assistants shall know the ties, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two fire-bars;
and let them be tightly bound, the fire-bars as we have said, and the physician shall place his palms firmly on the spine, until it heals.
