dislocations of the hip
Know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder are not dislocated except by dislocation only, nor do they come as other joints do; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and little out of place in front and back.
And the recognition of its internal dislocation is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears larger than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee over the fire. and is the place that is next to inflamed abscesses due to the fact that the hip's joint comes there.
And the sign of someone where it comes to a lack, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
And the sign of someone where it comes before, is that they stretch their leg well according to its completion; however, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants them to walk, they cannot move forward, and they retain their urine, and their ankles become swollen, and when they walk, they step on their heels.
And the sign of someone where it comes after, is that they cannot stretch their knee, or bend it, and this leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankles are swollen, and the hip joint is located under the ribs.[STHAGENITUS, De natura rerum (On the Nature of Things)]:
The method for reducing this type of dislocation is to consider whether the dislocation is old and remains in its position, in which case there is no need for treatment, nor should one presume to do anything. [STHAGENITUS, De natura rerum (On the Nature of Things)]:
And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, hasten to return the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee. and have another minister extend his hand in such a way that he places his hands under the patient's armpits, then squeeze the leg with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and let another hold the end of the ligament.[Translate request repeated from earlier comment.]
and extend upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground in one motion and remains hanging.[Translate request repeated from earlier comment.][Translate request repeated from earlier comment.]
This manner of stretching is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
If not, one must attend to its similarity. When the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh and the area beneath the groin, then pull the bandage up towards the groin and the armpit;
then take another person and have them hold the patient's arms while you embrace the affected thigh with both hands and stretch it outward significantly; this way, it should return to its proper place. This type of dislocation is easier to correct than others.
And if you cannot align it in this manner as we have described, then you should bind the patient's two feet together with a strong but soft ligament at the heels and the knees, and ensure that the affected leg is extended two fingers more than the healthy one.
then hang him by the head on a beam, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the thigh's head, and let another minister hang with the patient, who strongly embraces the thigh, for the joint returns quickly now.
And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten one ligament on the affected leg properly, and also on the foot.
then place two sticks, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert one stick between the patient's thighs, in the shape of a cross.[Original text uses "tisons" which means "firebrands", but context suggests that it refers to sticks or pieces of wood.] and have it wrapped with damp cloths to prevent injury to the patient, then each minister extends towards him, and the physician places his hand evenly on the dislocation.
If it returns (the dislocation), it is good. If not, place it on a table and press it as we have said in gilbosity, and let the patient lie on the sound side.
And when the dislocation is in front, the sickened leg should be quickly extended as I have said; and the physician should take care to be over the calf, then press with the other hand and stretch it downward toward the knee.
And if the dislocation is on the outside (defuer), the sickened part should not be stretched downward nor lifted up from the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated to the outside as we have said about lying on two hips.[5] The physician's goal is to realign the joint in its proper position, and excessive movement or force can cause further harm. Instead, the physician should carefully manipulate the limb into the correct position while causing minimal pain and damage to the patient. By understanding the anatomy of the hip joint and the mechanics of dislocation, a medieval physician could effectively treat this injury with a combination of careful observation, skilled manipulation, and knowledge of proper patient positioning. and let him be on his face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and pressure should be applied to the joint on the table.
and it will be time when the patient stretches out their legs and they are even; then adjust the hips, and apply the poultice, and strain a bandage around it, so that the swelling does not move.
and let him rest for 3 or 4 days, then loosen it and apply the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, strain it as before, and leave it for 3 days; then loosen it, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
of the dislocation of the knee.
The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; but never forward.[STH: I think the last sentence means "and it does not dislocate forwards."].
And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that it is dislocated.
and the restoration of all (dislocations) is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot upon your feet;
then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your hands, then firmly bend the two sides of the knee; and let another attendant stretch out his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily move his leg against his thigh.
and apply the poultice on it, and massage the leg against the thigh, and bind the limbs tightly together for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient must not exert himself to move, until the limb has regained its strength.
And if there is no feeling in the limb, apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of dropsy, until it has healed.
on dislocation of the ankle
The heels are sometimes dislocated, and at other times completely dislodged, both internally and externally.
And the signs of this are that the ankle is swollen, and it tilts towards the side where it is dislocated.
The reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.
And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and have one assistant hold them by the leg, above the ankle;
Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and properly place the foot up high;[IT] si que li chevilles soient plus hauz que les rotuns des fesses de .ii. dois;
and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it goes back into place, that is good; if not, then restart the procedure, for it will eventually go back.
and if it cannot be corrected in this way, have the patient lie down on their back on the ground, drive a stake firmly into the ground between their thighs, and tie a cloth around them so that they are not injured.
then one minister should hold the thigh, and another minister should extend the foot with their hands or a strap, tying it to the neck of the foot.[Additional context: This passage describes the steps to take if a dislocated joint cannot be corrected through pushing and pulling the limb. The patient is positioned on their back with a stake placed between their thighs for support. One minister holds the thigh in place while another extends the foot and ties it with a strap around the neck of the foot. This technique creates tension and may help to realign the dislocated joint.] then each minister should extend evenly, and the stake should remain between the patient's thighs to hold them in place as they are stretched.
then the surgeon should place both hands evenly on the dislocated joint, and another minister should hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocated joint will quickly return to its proper position.
And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight.
Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then unbind it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for four days; and if they go before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
And if abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.[Comment: The phrase "as we have said elsewhere" suggests that this treatise is a collection of writings on different medical topics, and the author refers to previous sections in the text. This also shows that the authors assume their readers have access to other parts of the work.]
of the shoulders
When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or leg, you should have the patient sit on a flat bed or table, upright, and place your foot on the visible part of the joint. Then press firmly with your foot until it returns to normal.[In this sentence, "nout" means "node," "part," or "joint" in modern French. It's used here to mean "any part of the back or leg."]
and when it is aligned and there's nothing visible, place a two-legged table under the sole of your foot, then strain it forcefully and leave it for three days. After that, release it and let the patient rest until they are healed.
about a wound and a dislocation together
When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to reset it, it often happens that the patient dies.
And do not be overconfident in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, and slow, not quick.
And at the beginning, use soothing remedies for a hot abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for their recovery. And when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place now, so that the hot abscess comes there.
And when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for the hot abscess and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments.
and if with the dislocation there is a break and small bones are separated, set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it will be fatal to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. Amen.
